fill="currentColor"></path></svg><span>Share</span></div></div></div><div class="space-y-8"><div><h1 class="text-2xl md:text-3xl font-semibold">Fog Ransomware – Technical Analysis</h1></div><div class="post-content">
<h1 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>what is Fog ?</strong></h1>



<p>In June [<a href="https://arcticwolf.com/resources/blog/lost-in-the-fog-a-new-ransomware-threat/">Arctic Wolf Labs</a>] reported a deployment of a new ransomware named Fog Ransomware,  according to their report the ransomware was seen in several incident Response cases, affecting education and recreation center in the United States, the investigation revealed that the attackers gain access to victims through compromised VPNs credentials, taking advantage of that , the Threat actors disabled Windows Defenders and deployed the ransomware, the reported file is an 32-bit EXE file with the hash <mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color has-black-color"><strong>83f00af43df650fda2c5b4a04a7b31790a8ad4cf</strong>,</mark> the below analysis was done by Dark Atlas Squad.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>Technical investigation</strong></h2>



<p>the ransomware was compiled using Microsoft Visual C/C++ by the end of April/24, also the developer used a lot of debug messages which were saved in a file called &#8220;DbgLog.sys&#8221; in the same directory of the ransomware process, the malware starts by the getting the address of kernel32.dll base address to resolve 2 APIs</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li>GetProcessHeap</li>



<li>HeapAlloc</li>
</ul>



<p>it traverse the PEB (Process Environment Block) and then go through Kernel32 memory to get the addresses of these APIs.</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/lqGvJui.png" alt="" style="width:728px;height:auto"/></figure></div>

<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/qQBrEWP.png" alt="" style="width:736px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<p>then the malware start loading another APIs dynamically using <strong><mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">GetProcAddress</mark></strong> and <strong><mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">LoadLibraryA</mark></strong> APIs , also it get the a handle to <strong><mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">ntdll.dll</mark></strong> which will be used to load native APIs, here is resolved APIs.</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li>HeapReAlloc</li>



<li>HeapFree</li>



<li>NtQuerySystemInformation</li>



<li>NtDuplicateObject</li>



<li>NtQueryObject</li>
</ul>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/RgNsEbC.png" alt="" style="width:673px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<p>the malware contain a lot of debugging msgs which is saved in file called <mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">Dbglog.sys</mark></p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/zCnXdpf.png" alt="" style="width:514px;height:auto"/></figure></div>

<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/mSMCb52.png" alt="" style="width:615px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>Malware Configuration</strong></h2>



<p>Ransomware configuration is decrypted and the malware decrypt it upon the execution, the configuration is saved in JSON format and after decryption it will try to parse it to extract its values and saves in allocated heap.<br>it will try to locate and save these values</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li>PathStopList</li>



<li>FileMaskStopList</li>



<li>ShutdownProcesses</li>



<li>ShutdownServices</li>



<li>RSAPubKey</li>



<li>LockedExt</li>



<li>NoteFileName</li>
</ul>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/FL2ngHb.png" alt="" style="width:689px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>File Encryption</strong></h2>



<p>Fog acts as a multi threading application by checking the number of processor to attach a thread for each core it uses <mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">GetSystemInfo</mark> and <mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">NtQuerySystemInformation</mark> to do so.</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/yoK5MJS.png" alt="" style="width:673px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<p>it creates a thread for each directory to work independent form other threads and for each directory it will drop the ransomware note.</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/pArGKOE.png" alt="" style="width:694px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>Crypto Initialization</strong></h2>



<p>FoG utilizes the Windows CryptoAPI to manage cryptographic contexts and import an RSA public key. It first attempts to acquire a cryptographic context using <strong><mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">CryptAcquireContextA</mark></strong>. <br>If this fails due to a missing key container <strong><mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">0x80090016</mark></strong>, it creates a new key container. Subsequently, it imports the RSA public key from a specified memory location using <mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">CryptImportKey</mark>. This process is essential for establishing secure communication channels or managing cryptographic keys, highlighting the importance of key handling in malware and secure application development.</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/UiymMJH.png" alt="" style="width:776px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>Stopping services</strong></h2>



<p>Fog will do the same as many ransomware did before by stopping a specific services that acts as obstacles for getting a read_write handle for some file, base on that For will try to stop these services.<br>it first gets a handle to service manager through calling <strong><mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">OpenSCManagerA</mark></strong> followed by a call to <strong><mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">EnumServciesStatusA</mark></strong> to get a list of active services</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/1ZJ8yOW.png" alt="" style="width:728px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<p>next it will check Pending services and then will start comparing active services names against the ones appeared on the malware configuration , it will compare each active services against the services list , if match happened it will get a handle to this service by calling <strong><mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">OpenServiceA</mark></strong>.</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/yxbvPOD.png" alt="" style="width:734px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<p>based on all of that it will call <strong><mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">ControlService</mark></strong> API to set the service in Stopping mode, by setting the second argument (dwControl) to this value &#8220;`SERVICE_CONTROL_STOP&#8220;`</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/9mRpnFA.png" alt="" style="width:745px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>Process Termination</strong></h2>



<p>Fog will also try to terminate a list of process if they are running on the infected system, it will get a list of the running process using CreateHealp32Snapshot, the it will go through this list using Process32First and Process32Next.</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/6q0CJk1.png" alt="" style="width:754px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<p>for each process it will access its name which is saved in <mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color"><strong>szExeFile</strong></mark> element in the <strong><mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">PROCESSENTRY32</mark></strong> structure which was retrieved by the above calls, it compare process name with the list of blacklisted process names saved on the malware configuration, and if a match found it will get a handle to this process using <strong><mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">OpenProcess</mark></strong> followed by a call to <strong><mark style="background-color:#fcb900" class="has-inline-color">TerminateProcess</mark></strong></p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/TgaEdQs.png" alt="" style="width:762px;height:auto"/></figure></div>

<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/JC73w98.png" alt="" style="width:764px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>Removing Backups</strong></h2>



<p>the malware will check if it is running inside a 32-bit or 64-bit system by using IsWow64Process API call.</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/ujzIHL5.png" alt="" style="width:762px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<p>&#8220;Sysnative&#8221; and &#8220;System32&#8221; are used to ensure the correct execution path for `vssadmin.exe` based on whether the system is 32-bit or 64-bit. This distinction is crucial for compatibility and proper command execution in different Windows environments.</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/zXPU5dr.png" alt="" style="width:724px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<p>it then will call &#8220;`SHEmptyRecycleBinA(0, 0, 7u); &#8220;` to delete all Recycle Bin elements. <br>and by the end of that it will log this message on the logging file</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="https://i.imgur.com/JEeZBXK.png" alt="" style="width:717px;height:auto"/></figure></div>


<p>we have tried to highlight the most important parts about this ransomware , wait for us for the upcoming in-detailed articles.</p>

class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eLoadLibraryA\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e APIs , also it get the a handle to \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003entdll.dll\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e which will be used to load native APIs, here is resolved APIs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cul class=\"wp-block-list\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eHeapReAlloc\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eHeapFree\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eNtQuerySystemInformation\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eNtDuplicateObject\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eNtQueryObject\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/RgNsEbC.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:673px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003cp\u003ethe malware contain a lot of debugging msgs which is saved in file called \u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eDbglog.sys\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large style=\"width:615px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003ch2 class=\"wp-block-heading\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMalware Configuration\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eRansomware configuration is decrypted and the malware decrypt it upon the execution, the configuration is saved in JSON format and after decryption it will try to parse it to extract its values and saves in allocated heap.\u003cbr\u003eit will try to locate and save these values\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cul class=\"wp-block-list\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePathStopList\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eFileMaskStopList\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eShutdownProcesses\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eShutdownServices\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eRSAPubKey\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eLockedExt\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eNoteFileName\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/FL2ngHb.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:689px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003ch2 class=\"wp-block-heading\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFile Encryption\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eFog acts as a multi threading application by checking the number of processor to attach a thread for each core it uses \u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eGetSystemInfo\u003c/mark\u003e and \u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eNtQuerySystemInformation\u003c/mark\u003e to do so.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/yoK5MJS.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:673px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eit creates a thread for each directory to work independent form other threads and for each directory it will drop the ransomware note.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/pArGKOE.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:694px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003ch2 class=\"wp-block-heading\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCrypto Initialization\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eFoG utilizes the Windows CryptoAPI to manage cryptographic contexts and import an RSA public key. It first attempts to acquire a cryptographic context using \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eCryptAcquireContextA\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e. \u003cbr\u003eIf this fails due to a missing key container \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003e0x80090016\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e, it creates a new key container. Subsequently, it imports the RSA public key from a specified memory location using \u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eCryptImportKey\u003c/mark\u003e. This process is essential for establishing secure communication channels or managing cryptographic keys, highlighting the importance of key handling in malware and secure application development.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/UiymMJH.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:776px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003ch2 class=\"wp-block-heading\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStopping services\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eFog will do the same as many ransomware did before by stopping a specific services that acts as obstacles for getting a read_write handle for some file, base on that For will try to stop these services.\u003cbr\u003eit first gets a handle to service manager through calling \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eOpenSCManagerA\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e followed by a call to \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eEnumServciesStatusA\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e to get a list of active services\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/1ZJ8yOW.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:728px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003cp\u003enext it will check Pending services and then will start comparing active services names against the ones appeared on the malware configuration , it will compare each active services against the services list , if match happened it will get a handle to this service by calling \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eOpenServiceA\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eControlService\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e API to set the service in Stopping mode, by setting the second argument (dwControl) to this value \u0026#8220;`SERVICE_CONTROL_STOP\u0026#8220;`\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/9mRpnFA.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:745px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003ch2 class=\"wp-block-heading\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eProcess Termination\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eFog will also try to terminate a list of process if they are running on the infected system, it will get a list of the running process using CreateHealp32Snapshot, the it will go through this list using Process32First and Process32Next.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/6q0CJk1.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:754px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003cp\u003efor each process it will access its name which is saved in \u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eszExeFile\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/mark\u003e element in the \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003ePROCESSENTRY32\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e structure which was retrieved by the above calls, it compare process name with the list of blacklisted process names saved on the malware configuration, and if a match found it will get a handle to this process using \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eOpenProcess\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e followed by a call to \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eTerminateProcess\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/ujzIHL5.png\" alt=\"\" ?\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h1\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eIn June [\u003ca href=\"https://arcticwolf.com/resources/blog/lost-in-the-fog-a-new-ransomware-threat/\"\u003eArctic Wolf Labs\u003c/a\u003e] reported a deployment of a new ransomware named Fog Ransomware,  according to their report the ransomware was seen in several incident Response cases, affecting education and recreation center in the United States, the investigation revealed that the attackers gain access to victims through compromised VPNs credentials, taking advantage of that , the Threat actors disabled Windows Defenders and deployed the ransomware, the reported file is an 32-bit EXE file with the hash \u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color has-black-color\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e83f00af43df650fda2c5b4a04a7b31790a8ad4cf\u003c/strong\u003e,\u003c/mark\u003e the below analysis was done by Dark Atlas Squad.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003ch2 class=\"wp-block-heading\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eTechnical investigation\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003ethe ransomware was compiled using Microsoft Visual C/C++ by the end of April/24, also the developer used a lot of debug messages which were saved in a file called \u0026#8220;DbgLog.sys\u0026#8221; in the same directory of the ransomware process, the malware starts by the getting the address of kernel32.dll base address to resolve 2 APIs\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cul class=\"wp-block-list\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eGetProcessHeap\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eHeapAlloc\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eit traverse the PEB (Process Environment Block) and then go through Kernel32 memory to get the addresses of these APIs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003entdll.dll\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e which will be used to load native APIs, here is resolved APIs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cul style=\"width:673px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003cp\u003ethe malware contain a lot of debugging msgs which is saved in file called \u003cmark Configuration\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eRansomware configuration is decrypted and the malware decrypt it upon the execution, the configuration is saved in JSON format and after decryption it will try to parse it to extract its values and saves in allocated heap.\u003cbr\u003eit will try to locate and save these values\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cul class=\"wp-block-list\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePathStopList\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eFileMaskStopList\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eShutdownProcesses\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eShutdownServices\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eRSAPubKey\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eLockedExt\u003c/li\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cli\u003eNoteFileName\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv Encryption\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eFog acts as a multi threading application by checking the number of processor to attach a thread for each core it uses \u003cmark class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eNtQuerySystemInformation\u003c/mark\u003e to do so.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/yoK5MJS.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:673px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eit creates a thread for each directory to work independent form other threads and for each directory it will drop the ransomware note.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/pArGKOE.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:694px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003ch2 class=\"wp-block-heading\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCrypto Initialization\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eFoG utilizes the Windows CryptoAPI to manage cryptographic contexts and import an RSA public key. It first attempts to acquire a cryptographic context using \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eCryptAcquireContextA\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e. \u003cbr\u003eIf this fails due to a missing key container \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003e0x80090016\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e, it creates a new key container. Subsequently, it imports the RSA public key from a specified memory location using \u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eCryptImportKey\u003c/mark\u003e. This process is essential for establishing secure communication channels or managing cryptographic keys, highlighting the importance of key handling in malware and secure application development.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/UiymMJH.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:776px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003ch2 class=\"wp-block-heading\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStopping services\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eFog will do the same as many ransomware did before by stopping a specific services that acts as obstacles for getting a read_write handle for some file, base on that For will try to stop these services.\u003cbr\u003eit first gets a handle to service manager through calling \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eOpenSCManagerA\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e followed by a call to \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eEnumServciesStatusA\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e to get a list of active services\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/1ZJ8yOW.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:728px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003cp\u003enext it will check Pending services and then will start comparing active services names against the ones appeared on the malware configuration , it will compare each active services against the services list , if match happened it will get a handle to this service by calling \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eOpenServiceA\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/yxbvPOD.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:734px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003cp\u003ebased on all of that it will call \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eControlService\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e API to set the service in Stopping mode, by setting the second argument (dwControl) to this value \u0026#8220;`SERVICE_CONTROL_STOP\u0026#8220;`\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/9mRpnFA.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:745px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003ch2 class=\"wp-block-heading\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eProcess Termination\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003eFog will also try to terminate a list of process if they are running on the infected system, it will get a list of the running process using CreateHealp32Snapshot, the it will go through this list using Process32First and Process32Next.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/6q0CJk1.png\" alt=\"\" style=\"width:754px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003cp\u003efor each process it will access its name which is saved in \u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eszExeFile\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/mark\u003e element in the \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003ePROCESSENTRY32\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e structure which was retrieved by the above calls, it compare process name with the list of blacklisted process names saved on the malware configuration, and if a match found it will get a handle to this process using \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eOpenProcess\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e followed by a call to \u003cstrong\u003e\u003cmark style=\"background-color:#fcb900\" class=\"has-inline-color\"\u003eTerminateProcess\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large style=\"width:764px;height:auto\"/\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\n\n\u003ch2 class=\"wp-block-heading\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRemoving Backups\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\n\n\n\u003cp\u003ethe malware will check if it is running inside a 32-bit or 64-bit system by using IsWow64Process API call.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"\u003e\u003cimg decoding=\"async\" src=\"https://i.imgur.com/ujzIHL5.png\" alt=\"\" execution path for `vssadmin.exe` based on whether the system is 32-bit or 64-bit. This distinction is crucial for compatibility and proper command execution in different Windows environments.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"wp-block-image\"\u003e\n\u003cfigure
